This series contains materials about the Logan ranch in St. Ignatius, Montana. It includes material on agricultural practices, buildings, cattle crops, and well drilling, but mostly concerns the leases and activities of tenants that rented the ranch while the Logans lived in Illinois.
This series contains primarily Logan family photographs and images of S. Rae Logan. They are mostly well-identified and include his ancestors, parents, siblings, early Montana and North Carolina scenes, his college days in Chapel Hill, the St. Ignatius, Montana, ranch and surrounding areas, District #28 and Winnetka Schools scenes, and images from Hardin, Montana.
S. R. Logan second from right, front row. File also contains North Carolina currency from Civil War.
This collection includes transcribed letters that date from Sept. 21, 1856 to Dec. 13, 1914. Most of the correspondence takes place amongst Roy Cobban and his family. The largest part of the collection is a group of letters beginning in December 1885 detailing a developing relationship between Roy Cobban and Alice Hardy. Roy Cobban wrote a series of letters to his mother that served as a diary of his journey to Western Montana from Wisconsin and also detailed his business ventures until 1886. There are several replies from his mother. Miscellaneous letters include ones written by William S. Cobban to his brother John and his brother Alexander, an unsigned letter written to an unidentified wife, a letter recommending Robert Cobban for employment, and a letter written in 1914 addressed to parents from Lulu.
The collection contains the financial and legal records of the Northwestern Live Stock Company. There are a complete set of corporate minutes from 1901 to 1941, that document board of director's meetings, stock issuance, capitalization, and reorganizations. Interspersed with other financial records are immunization records, herd counts, and livestock sales. Many of the legal records concern land leases, purchases, transfers, and negotiation of grazing permits with the U.S. Forest Service. The earliest land records appear in abstracts of title attached to later documents.
This collection contains correspondence relating to the creation and administration of the Historical Society of Western Montana as well as meeting minutes and publications from other organizations on starting and operating local historical societies from 1954 to 1955.
Letter from Forest Service Chief H.S. Graves, to Elers Koch and the Region One forest officers, November 7, 1910; letter from H.P. Barringer to Henry J. Claffey, November 8, 1910; and H.P. Barringer's report on the 1910 Grave Creek/Trout Creek Fire, November 8, 1910.
This collection represents a large portion of the academic research and writing career of Fred W. Voget from his undergraduate years in the 1930s to a few years before his death in 1997. While the bulk of his research was focused on the Crow Tribe, the collection also includes secondary source research on numerous other North American tribes and primary source research on the Iroquois, Shoshoni, and Blackfeet Indians. Research specific to the Crow Tribe includes bibliographies, annotated photocopies of papers, book chapters, and articles, interviews spanning half of century from 1939 to 1993, and photographs from 1939 to 1987
This series includes notes and readings on anthropology theory and practice, bibliographies of anthropology readings, and a small amount of anthropology research notes. Additionally, the series has reading notes and bibliographies on a number of Native American tribes. The arbitrary arrangement begins with general anthropology and moves into broad Native American topics.
This series includes bibliographies, research notes on readings, annotated and clean copies of materials, newspaper articles, contact information, and interview notes. The bulk of the series is Crow Indian research, but material such as interviews with Shoshoni tribe members have been included to duplicate Voget's synthesis of this research in his book The Shoshoni-Crow Sun Dance. While the broad order of this series is arbitrary, Voget's original card file order has been maintained. Cards in "to be filed" groups were filed according to established categories and notes not on cards have been inserted into separate folders according to those same categories or topics. Groupings of interviews have been maintained as much as possible.
This series includes Voget's handwritten field research notebooks on the Shoshoni, the Iroquois, the Blackfeet, and the Crow. Many parts of the notebooks are written in shorthand. The Iroquois and Blackfeet notebooks were transcribed in 2003 and 2004.
This series includes a small amount of language research notes from secondary sources, but the bulk of the series consists of handwritten and typed cards with a word or phrase in English and the corresponding Crow word or phrase with pronunciation markings.
This series includes some of Voget's undergraduate papers, working drafts of articles and book chapters, and copies of published articles. The drafts preceded published works and probably a planned history of the Crow Indians that was not published at the time of processing.
This series includes Voget's photos, slides, and some negatives taken throughout his research. The bulk of the photos chronicle Crow activities such as the sun dance and arrow throw, feasts, and giveaways. A smaller number of photos are of specific individuals significant to Crow history and/or Voget's research. Another small group of photos pertain to Native American artifacts, the Shoshoni sun dance, and to Mohawk and other Six Nations groups. Most of the photos are very usable with the exception of photos 25/75 through 25/89, which are out of focus. Original photo captions and photo groupings were maintained where they existed. Otherwise, the photos in this series are arranged in rough thematic and chronological order. The slides are grouped at the end of this series.
In 2012, additional or corrected information for some photographs and context about places and events was provided by Aaron Brien, a member of the Apsaalooke Nation, in consultation with other members of the Nation. This information was added with the preface [From Aaron Brien]. When a date was corrected, the correct date was placed in the date field.
Digital copies of the materials in Box 20/Folder 30 through Box 26 are available online at https://umt.box.com/v/Mss318FredWVogetPapers. These digital copies were created in 2009 and are meant for reference only.
The collection contains the company's governing documents, financial records, correspondence, legal documents and court papers, reports, clippings, publicity and printed materials, and photographs.
This series contains documentation on the governance and history of the company. It includes corporate histories written within and without the company, founding documents (articles of incorporation, resolutions), and some minutes of Board of Directors meetings, mostly from the earliest years of the company.
This series contains incoming and outgoing correspondence from the company.
This series contains the company's financial records, including those related to taxes, stockholders, unemployment compensation, operating statements, general ledgers, check stubs, ledgers, and journals. There are also some of Thomas Sidwell's personal financial materials.
This series contains court papers related to a 1956-1960 case, Gadsden vs. New Mine Sapphire Syndicate. At issue were Gadsden's assets after her husband, Charles T. Gadsden (a New Sapphire manager of many years) died in 1954.
This series contains legal documents, including deeds, patents, and materials related to the company's mining claims.
This series consists of one folder of reports produced or commissioned by the New Mine Sapphire Syndicate. Most relate to mining claims.
This series consists of two folders of maps and blueprints related to the operations of the New Mine Sapphire Syndicate. Some relate to mining claims, and others are unidentified.
This series contains newspaper and magazine clippings, mostly from Montana publications, about the Yogo sapphires.
This series contains printed and other publicity materials produced by and for the company.
This series contains photographs of the New Mine Sapphire Syndicate operation in Utica, Montana. Most were taken around 1924-1925, and show the buildings, mechanicals, and other aspects of the mine site and mining equipment. Several images show damage after floods.
This collection contains information on Barbara Evans’ twenty-eight year political career as a Missoula County Commissioner in Missoula, Montana. The collection contains newspaper clippings, correspondence, campaign and election materials, photographs, awards, press releases, scrapbooks, and posters that convey political happenings both directly and indirectly related to Evans’ political career. The bulk of the material is newspaper clippings. The collection highlights some of Evans political achievements including her work on the Reserve Street expansion, her efforts to remove the Milltown Dam, involvement in numerous housing, industrial, and infrastructure developments, as well as some of her political controversies that included her clash with democratic commissioners Bob Palmer and Germaine Conrad.
This series consists of newspaper clippings, correspondence, campaign and election materials, photographs, awards, press releases, and posters.
This series consists of scrapbooked news clippings, correspondence, campaign and election materials, photographs, press releases, speeches, and awards related to Evans career and Missoula County politics during her time as a county commissioner. The scrapbooks contain both integrated and loose materials. All scrapbooks contain undated material.
This collection contains correspondence to Whicker from magazine editors regarding the printing of original works by Whicker. These include letters from Doubleday, Fiction Parade, Story, and the Atlantic Monthly. The letters also track Whicker's many residences in the Northwest from Marshfield, Oregon to Guemes Island, Washington. One of the works referenced in the correspondence is an unpublished novel titled Cardiac Island. Also included in the collection are copies of works mentioned in the correspondence. Specifically, these include a copy of an essay titled "The Spirit of the Game," printed in Scribner's Magazine in 1929 and two stories. One story is "All-American," reprinted in Fiction Parade in 1936, and the other is "Voyageur," printed in Story in 1935.
This collection includes photocopies of letters written by Alicia Conrad to George Campbell prior to their marriage in February 1928. At the time of the first letter Alicia Conrad was thirty-four years old, from a well-respected Montana family, and a divorcee with a school-age daughter. The tone of her early letters is playful and flirtatious. In a later letter she mentions the stress of her divorce and later still her concern about Campbell's father's opinion of her. According to one letter, even Timmie posed a problem for the couple's happiness as the child misbehaved around Campbell. Still, Conrad expresses great happiness at the developing relationship.
This collection details the initial steps taken by the Rexford Townsite Company to set up the original townsite of Rexford, Montana, as well as a few records of later town activities. The collection includes limited general correspondence, legal documents such as articles of incorporation and deeds and lot contracts, townsite sales ledger, accounting records of both receipts and expenses. Most material is from 1903 when the townsite was actually set up, although miscellaneous details dragged on into 1907. Major exceptions include the Rexford Athletic Association Book from 1912 and a precinct register from 1911-1912.
This Series includes the Rexford Townsite Company general correspondence (limited), articles of incorporation, deeds and lot contracts for various sites in Rexford, a rough pencil drawing of street layout, receipts, invoices, canceled checks, a cashbook, a ledger, townsite sales ledger, and a stock ledger.
This Series includes a Rexford Athletic Association book which holds brief minutes for two meetings in April, 1912, and nine receipts for bills paid in 1912. This Series also includes the 1911-1912 precinct record book for Rexford as the 9th precinct of Lincoln County.
This record group contains correspondence, budget records, general store records, scrapbooks, miscellaneous materials, general ASUM meeting minutes, Central Board Meeting Minutes and other records generated from 1906-2010.
The Associated Student’s Store was started in 1922 by two students. The first store was a table by the psychology building (then the Law Building). The original stock consisted of pens, pencils, and candy. The store then grew and moved into the “Shack” behind Main Hall, where the continued to sell supplies, candy, and a small concessions area with sandwiches. With the student population continuing to grow, the Associated Student’s store soon outgrew their space and moved into the basement of the present day Fine Arts building in 1937. The store was disincorporated from the university in the early 1950s, but reincorporated when University of Montana President McFarland left office. The store moved into the second floor of the Lodge (now the Emma Lommasson Center) in 1954, then into the new base of operations in the University Center when the building was constructed in 1969.
This collection consists of David Bentzin’s copies of reports, files, and documents related to Docket 279-D of the Indian Claims Commission case of the Blackfeet Tribe of Montana vs. The United States of America in the 1970s. Bentzin acted as an expert witness for the Blackfeet Tribe in his capacity as a petroleum exploration geologist. Researchers will find Bentzin’s annotations on a few reports.
This collection contains financial, organizational, correspondence, promotional, and reference materials generated by the First National Bank of Missoula and a small sample of financial records from the Missoula Trust and Savings Bank. Collection materials significantly document Missoula's early economic history, the town's foundational business relationships, the ebb and flow of western Montana economic development from the late nineteenth century through the early twentieth century, the impacts of national procedural/regulatory changes upon rural banks, and daily operations at the Missoula institution.
This series contains outgoing and incoming correspondence regarding First National Bank operations. Correspondence sequences are relatively complete from 1873 to 1900; however, significant gaps exist after 1900 and the sequence ends in 1921. This series also includes one file of correspondence with K. Ross Toole, dated 1965. This file documents K. Ross Toole's efforts to secure the collection for the Archives, an instructional essay written by Toole regarding archival processing in Montana, and transcriptions of letters from the S.T. Hauser collection at the Montana State Historical Society he deemed relevant to the First National Bank collection.
This series contains three documents relating to the incorporation of the First National Bank. Included is a copy of the 1866 Articles of Incorporation for the First National Bank of Helena, Montana (used as a template for the Missoula National Bank's articles of incorporation), a copy of the 1873 Articles of Incorporation for the Missoula National Bank, and a 1913 amendment to the First Nationa Montana Bank of Missoula's Articles of Incorporation. These materials document the early organization of one of western Montana's first corporate ventures.
This series contains financial records from the First National Bank, primarily bound ledgers. Materials include general operating ledgers, individual account records, daily balance logs, regulatory reports of assets and liabilities, cash and credit transaction documents, and client signature books. Federal records include reports to and notices from the U.S. Treasury Department. Materials in this series present significant documentation of Missoula's early economic history, the town's foundational business relationships, the ebb and flow of western Montana economic development from the late nineteenth century through the early twentieth century, the impacts of national procedural/regulatory changes upon rural banks, and daily operations at the Missoula institution.
This series contains three newspaper scrapbooks detailing developments within the First National Bank from 1903-1939, samples of internal forms, and two examples of Bank promotional materials. The items in this series provide broad insights into First National Bank operations and public relations.
This series contains financial records from the Missoula Trust and Savings Bank. The exact relationship between Missoula Trust and Savings Bank and the First National Bank is not established by collection materials.
This collection contains general correspondence, financial records, legal documents, clippings, and miscellany. Included are personal letters, 1893-1972; records of household finances, 1946-1957; income tax forms, 1936-1972; certificates, 1887-1935; memorial records, 1966-1972; and newspaper clippings. Two letters to the MacIvors dated Jan. 21, 1922 and February 8, 1922, give details of an automobile trip from Butte, Montana to Portland, Oregon. Two folders of previously unincorporated photographs were added into the collection in 2006.
This series includes early personal correspondence to Nell and her sister, Eliza, from both their brother, Asa Crockett, and father, Daniel W. Crockett. There is later personal correspondence between Nell and Donald MacIvor. A few letters concern Mr. MacIvor's attempt to get a temporary release from the railroad in 1918 in order to gain an officer's commission in the army. Instead of gaining an officer's commission, Mr. MacIvor became chairman of the United War Campaign which raised funds for the war effort. Folder 2 contains a practice exam given to immigrants who desired United States citizenship. This folder also includes two letters describing an automobile trip from Butte, Montana to Portland, Oregon in 1921. Folder 3 contains a description of a trip to Jerusalem from Beirut in 1951 and other correspondence to the MacIvors describing life in the Middle East in the 1950s.
This series contains records of the MacIvor's household finances while living in Missoula from 1944-1957. Examples of expenses included furnace oil, electric lights, and rent. A primary source of income was Mr. MacIvor's railroad pension. The second folder contains the MacIvor's state and federal income tax forms from 1936-1972.
This series contains Nell's birth certificate, high school diploma, and a Diploma of Progress from the Methodist Episcopal Church. It also includes Donald's Military Registration Certificate, Notice of Military Classification, and membership cards for the Liberty Loan Committee.
This series primarily includes newspaper clippings about Judge Asa James Crockett, who was related to Nell.
This series contains a memorial book for Judge Asa James Crockett who died in 1966. This book includes a brief family history. There is also a memorial for Nell MacIvor, who died in 1972. There is an address book and two valentines. The valentines were sent to Nell from Donald dated circa 1907.
Photographs include formal portraits and snapshots of people and scenes, including images from the Bearmouth, Montana, and Hopewell, Nova Scotia.
This is a collection of newsletters, handbooks, and pamphlets. It includes copies of the annual MIEA handbook, which was prepared jointly by the University of Montana School of Journalism and MIEA and served as a directory of publications and publication advisors at Montana high schools. The collection also contains copies of the MIEA newsletter, The Editor, from 1957 to 1975 which was published several times during the school year. The MIEA advisor, often a faculty member of the Journalism School, served as editor of the newsletter.
This collection is divided into four series.
Series I: Correspondence (1919-1985) The bulk of the correspondence is letters to Clarice Cushman from her husband, William Cushman, when he was away from home in the U.S. Navy during WWII, in Liberia for four years, in the Warm Springs mental health facility in Montana, and in the Veterans Hospital in Sheridan, Wyoming. The letters chronicle the family’s daily lives, the centrality of religious beliefs, marital discord, and four decades of Clarice Cushman’s attempts to find medical and education assistance for their son, Roger Cushman, who had severe disabilities. The correspondence also includes letters from relatives, friends and institutions, letters received by William Cushman, and letters received by Roger Cushman.
Series II: Diaries and Scrapbooks (1920-1971) includes Clarice Cushman’s diaries, that begin a few years before her marriage to William Cushman in 1935 and end during WWII. Her sometimes daily brief entries reveal her daily activities, social contacts, and later interactions with her husband. The more sporadic entries in William Cushman’s diaries describe his work and include one lengthier examination of his feelings about his marriage and his wife while they are apart. Clarice Cushman’s scrapbook (1920-1925) contains photos and memorabilia of her school years beginning in high school and ending when she is awarded a teaching certificate. The other two scrapbooks of local music and school events may have been done as an exercise with the Cushman’s son, Roger.
Series III: Financial Records (1928-1968) consists of a few scattered bank records and some daily and weekly income and expenditure lists.
Series IV: Miscellaneous (1918-1974) consists of memorabilia from high school, weddings, and births as well as various types of personal identification, a genealogy, church programs, and religious tracts. The few identified photos are of the Cushmans around the late 1930s.
The collection consists of Garlington's papers from the 1972 Montana Constitutional Convention. It contains a daily journal kept by Garlington, his campaign expenditures and some speeches, legal material dealing with the election recount, newspaper articles on the Convention and Missoula delegates, a copy of the Montana revised codes, and correspondence between Garlington and others. Publications in the collection concern the drafting of state constitutions. A voter's guide has short biographies of all Convention delegates.
From the Convention itself are draft proposals and letters of transmittal from committees on the executive, education, natural resource and agriculture, judicial committees, and legislative committees. Also contained in the collection are various member proposals, educational material sponsored by the Society of American Foresters and Office of Public Instruction, a resolution calling for submittal of the proposed constitution to the voters, and highlights of the proposed constitution.
This series contains the journal that Garlington kept throughout the Convention, and consists mainly of his notes on each day's events. It includes many copies of minutes, proposals, and other inserts.
This series contains Garlington's correspondence related to the Convention. It contains letters congratulating him on his election, requests to focus on particular issues, and other matters.
This series contains records of Garlington's election, including campaign materials, speeches, the recount challenge, and the financial records from the campaign.
This series contains materials from the Convention, including the activities of committees. It also contains Garlington's appointment certificate and materials about the Convention delegates.
This series contains clippings from Montana newspapers about the Convention and its activities.
This collection is an original charter from the National Farmers' Alliance authorizing the formation of the Carlton Farmers’ Alliance No.6, in Stevensville, Montana, on December 17, 1890.
The Boone and Crockett Club Records have been divided into six Series, most of which have been further subdivided. The largest series in this collection is Series I: Administration, which contains early administrative correspondence and Executive Committee minutes, almost an entire run of the minutes of the Club’s annual meetings which began in 1893, and an almost complete run of Officer, Committee, and Membership booklets which were produced by the Club each year.
This collection also includes materials documenting the Club’s involvement in the big game conservation history of North America including general correspondence, Game Preservation Committee and Conservation Committee meeting minutes and correspondence, and materials documenting the Boone and Crockett Club’s Conservation Grants Program. The collection also contains materials that relate to the Boone and Crockett Club’s big game records keeping activities. These materials include documents pertaining to North American Big Game Records Competitions and Awards Programs, Records of North American Big Game Committee meeting minutes and correspondence files, the materials produced by the administrative staff of the Club’s Big Game Records Division, and materials related to the National Collection of Heads and Horns. Additionally, the records include documents related to the Boone and Crockett Club’s publications including administrative correspondence, planning materials and drafts of the Club’s records books, and drafts and correspondence related to the Club’s Fair Chase magazine.
This series contains materials related to the administrative division of the Boone and Crockett Club, including general correspondence, officer and committee reports, meeting minutes, and materials related to the Club’s annual and other member meetings. The Series has been divided into twelve subseries, most of which have been subdivided further into sub-subseries.
Materials were grouped and interfiled by the processor to reflect the historic and current organization of the Club’s administration. Series are arranged alphabetically.
This subseries contains drafts of the Club’s constitution, by-laws, and incorporation. It documents the evolution of the Club’s by-laws as it contains correspondence regarding amendments and proposed changes dating from 1922 through 1993. Additionally, the series contains drafts and proposed amendments of the Club’s constitution and documents the evolution of the Club’s statement of purpose.
This subseries contains a run of general correspondence that documents the grassroots development of the Club. Although correspondence before 1891 that would document the founding of the Club is missing from the collection, early incoming and outgoing correspondence by founding Club members George Bird Grinnell and Theodore Roosevelt is included in this subseries. Additionally, the subseries contains materials that document the Club’s organizational development. Although this early correspondence does document the Club’s involvement in conservation and publications, specific correspondence regarding these subjects and big game records can be found in Series’ II, III, and IV.
This subseries contains annual reports, ledgers, financial statements and correspondence, budget and tax materials, and materials related to bequests, gifts and legacies left to the Club by members in their wills. Materials such as cancelled checks, invoices and receipts dated post-1950 have been removed from the collection.
This subseries is divided into 3 sub-subseries and contains materials generated by the Executive Officers of the Club as well as other administrative committees. Materials include meeting minutes, correspondence, and reports.
This sub-series contains correspondence and reports created by individual members in their capacity as Executive Officers. The files arrived at the archives in folders which appear to contain materials from a single member and be limited to that member’s work as an officer of the Club. This sub-subseries was created to reflect that organization and original order within folders was maintained. Folders are arranged alphabetically by a member’s last name and present an almost complete picture of the role of Executive officers in the Boone and Crockett Club.
The executive committee of the Boone and Crockett Club was responsible for the general administration of the Club in conjunction with executive officers. This sub-subseries contains an almost entire run of executive committee meeting minutes dating from the Club’s earliest official meeting in 1888 through 2000. The Club would eventually transition from an executive committee to a board of directors, as is the current administrative organization.
This sub-subseries contains administrative committee materials not created by the executive committee. Materials include correspondence, minutes, and reports.
Annual membership gatherings have been a cornerstone of the Club since its inception. The founding members believed that meetings and discussions between members kept the membership active and engaged in conservation issues. This subseries has been divided into three sub-subseries.
This sub-subseries contains the minutes of over 100 years of the Club’s annual meetings, which document membership involvement in the conservation, big game records keeping, and foundation goals of the Club.
This sub-subseries includes planning materials, correspondence, and committee materials related to the Club’s Centennial Celebration which took place in 1988 in Dallas, Texas.
In addition to the Club’s annual meetings, membership was often invited to attend casual meetings throughout the year. In the early years of the Club these meetings included presentations and slideshows of hunts by individual members. Later, the Club moved to have membership officially meet quarterly. This sub-subseries contains meeting minutes, correspondence, and planning materials for these events.
This subseries contains minutes, correspondence, member mailers, membership election ballots, and Membership Committee materials. The subseries includes almost an entire run of Club yearbooks which document Club membership, officers, and committee involvement dating from 1906 to the present. The subseries also documents the process for obtaining regular membership as it includes membership endorsements and sponsorships.
This subseries contains correspondence, appraisals, and inventories pertaining to the Club library that contains materials owned by the Roosevelt family and gifted to the Club by other members.
This subseries includes correspondence, committee materials and minutes, inventories and materials and plans related to the purchase and remodel of the Old Milwaukee Railroad Depot (the Club’s current headquarters in Missoula, Montana). Of possible interest in this series are materials documenting the ownership of Guns gifted to the Club by the Roosevelt family and currently stored at the Sagamore Hill National Historic Site in Oyster Bay, New York.
This subseries contains committee minutes, correspondence, and materials related to various unpublished histories written about the Club. This subseries also contains materials related to the Oral History project started by the Club to document its history through interviews with longtime members.
This subseries includes drafts and copies of dedications, eulogies, speeches, and other statements given by Club members.
This subseries is divided into two sub-subseries and documents the administration of Club offices.
Sub sub-series 1 includes office policies, stationary, general inquiries and other materials related to office administration. Of particular interest in this sub-subseries are folders that document the move of the Club’s headquarters from Pittsburgh to Virginia and from Virginia to Montana.
Beginning in 1981, the Club employed an administrative director and the position changed title to executive director by 1985. This sub-subseries contains correspondence generated by office administrators and executive directors of the Club. Correspondence from professional staff employed in the big game records and publications divisions of the Club is filed in series III and IV respectively.
This subseries contains articles, clippings, correspondence, and additional materials.
Since its inception, the Boone and Crockett Club has been actively involved in conservation issues. This series documents the Club’s conservation activity from its early efforts to preserve game habitat through present-day efforts to fund educational activities. This series has been divided into five subseries and includes committee meeting minutes, correspondence, conservation grant requests and progress reports, and materials related to collaborative efforts and campaigns. Included in this series are materials related to the Club’s concept of Fair Chase.
Materials were grouped and interfiled by the processor to reflect the historic and current organization of the Club’s conservation efforts. Series are arranged alphabetically.
This subseries documents the conservation efforts of the Boone and Crockett Club that took place before the Conservation Committee was formed in 1947. Materials include correspondence, meeting minutes and reports from the Game Preservation Committee (of which George Bird Grinnell was chair) which documents the Club’s involvement in the designation of Glacier and Mt. McKinley National Parks. Also included are materials related to the Club’s conservation positions and policies. Absent are documents related to the Club’s involvement in conservation activities before 1904.
The Conservation Committee of the Boone and Crockett Club was formed in 1947 to address the Club’s conservation policies and actions. Various subcommittees were organized throughout the existence of the Conservation Committee and by 1994 the committee would include three standing sub-committees; one that oversaw the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch, one that worked with the Club’s university professorship programs, and one that oversaw grants-in-aid. By 1998, the Club had reorganized its committees and created the Hunter and Conservation Ethics Committee and the Position Papers Committee. The Ranch subcommittee, Professorship subcommittee and Grants-in-aid subcommittee became full committees. This subseries has been divided into four sub-subseries reflecting the work of the Conservation Committee.
Of particular interest within this sub-subseries is an almost complete run of the Conservation Committee’s correspondence and reports from 1947 through 1991. This sub-subseries also contains materials documenting the Club’s efforts to assist in the support of game refuges including their assistance in the creation of the Key Deer Refuge in Florida. Additionally, this sub-subseries contains a print designed by cartoonist and Club member Jay Norwood “Ding” Darling after the designation of the Key Deer Refuge.
This sub-subseries contains grant proposals, project reports, and grants-in-aid subcommittee meeting minutes. The sub-subseries documents the research the Club supported from 1959 through 2001, including early Isle Royale Wolf Research and Predator-Prey studies. Absent are materials documenting Club grant-in-aid support for projects between the late 1940s and 1959.
This Sub-subseries contains applications, correspondence, proposals and progress reports related to the Club’s Conservation Grants Program. The materials also include correspondence, and review materials created by the Grants-in-Aid subcommittee, a subcommittee of the Conservation Committee. These materials arrived at the archives in 2011, after other Conservation Grant files had been organized. The 2011 addition arrived arranged chronologically by the Boone and Crockett Club. This order was maintained, as was original order within folders.
This sub-subseries documents the development of Boone and Crockett conservation workshops of the 1970s. This sub-subseries demonstrates the Club’s national and international involvement and collaboration in conservation. Of particular interest in this sub-subseries are materials documenting the Club’s involvement in the National Forest System Centennial Celebration and the National Wildlife Conservation Partners Summit that was hosted by the Club.
This sub-subseries contains articles, clippings, correspondence, and additional materials.
The idea of fair chase was first proposed by Theodore Roosevelt and was present in the original Club constitution. It prohibited “killing bear or cougar in traps, crusting moose, elk or deer in deep snow, jacking, or killing them from a boat.” This subseries documents the evolution of the Club’s Fair Chase policy from the early 1960s through the late 1990s.
This subseries also includes materials related to the Club’s positions on a wide variety of topics from gun control, private property rights, and animal rights to the reintroduction of the wolf in Yellowstone National Park. Researchers will find materials documenting the development of these positions as well as responses from Club members to the Club’s position papers.
This subseries contains correspondence, endorsements, and additional materials related to conservation awards given to Club members as well as conservation awards given by the Club.
This subseries contains correspondence, promotional packets, catalogs and mailers related to the Club’s conservation and fundraising campaigns. Included here are materials related to the Club’s conservation stamp print fundraising effort as well as the Blazing New Trails for Conservation campaign.
This series documents the Club’s big game records activities including the evolution of the management of the Big Game Records program as well as materials related to Official Measurers, the Sagamore Hill Medal Program, and the National Collection of Heads and Horns. This series has been divided into five subseries and includes committee meeting minutes, correspondence, Awards Program planning materials, menus, invitations and trophy certificates, as well as correspondence and inventories related to the National Collection of Heads and Horns.
Materials in this series arrived at the archives with no discernable original order and were grouped and interfiled by the processor to reflect historic and current organization of the Club’s big game records keeping activities and management. Series are arranged alphabetically and original order within folders was maintained.
Note: Trophy records and related photographs are maintained at the Boone and Crockett Club headquarters in their Big Game Records Department.
This subseries has been divided into three subseries and documents the administration of the club’s big game records program. Established in 1935, the Records of North American Big Game Committee supervised the Big Game Competitions until the Club began collaborating on Big Game Records with the National Rifle Association in 1973. At that time, the administrative duties fell to the North American Big Game Awards Program, which was housed in the Hunting Activities Department of the National Rifle Association. Currently, Big Game Records are administered in collaboration with the North American Big Game Committee and professional staff.
This subseries is divided into three sub-subseries which reflect the evolution of the management of Big Game Records at the Boone and Crockett Club.
This sub-subseries contains materials related to committee involvement in Big Game Records keeping.
Sub-sub-subseries 1 includes materials produced by the Records of North American big Game Committee. In the years from 1935 through 1973, the Committee managed and oversaw the Club’s big game records-keeping efforts including the North American Big Game Awards Programs. Of particular interest are correspondence to and from Grancel and Betty Fitz that documents changes in the trophy scoring system. Additionally, this sub-sub-subseries contains meeting minutes, correspondence, trophy score sheets and materials related to scoring from 1939 through 1993. Absent are correspondence or meeting minutes created by the Committee before 1944.
Sub-sub-subseries 2 includes materials created by the Friends of North American Big Game Committee, a group that financially supported the North American Big Game Committee through subscriptions from the early 1950s through the early 1960s. Materials include correspondence, big game census figures and subscription information.
Sub-sub-subseries 3 includes materials produced by ad hoc committees related to Big Game Records. This sub-sub-subseries contains correspondence, memorandum and score chart revisions. Of particular interest are materials related to the development of the trophy scoring system by Samuel B. Webb that took place in the late 1940s and early 1950s. It is this scoring system that became the standard for big game trophy measurement after its development and is still in use today.
The North American Big Game Awards Program was a joint venture between the Boone and Crockett Club and the National Rifle Association to administer the Club’s big game records keeping responsibilities and Awards Programs. The North American Big Game Awards Program was in existence from 1973 through late 1980, when the partnership dissolved.
This Sub-subseries contains meeting minutes, correspondence, trophy score sheets and materials related to scoring.
This Sub-subseries contains materials created by the professional staff tasked with administering the Club’s Big Game Records program first in conjunction with the National Rifle Association, and since 1980, with the Boone and Crockett Club’s Records of North American Big Game Committee. Materials include correspondence with trophy owners as well as the Records of North American Big Game Committee and the National Rifle Association.
The materials in this Sub-subseries document the evolution of the Club’s Big Game Records program from being administered solely by members acting as volunteers to that of a partnership between paid staff and Club Committee members.
This Boone and Crockett Club has held North American Big Game Awards Programs since 1947. This Subseries contains materials from the first North American Big Game Competition in 1947 through the 24th North American Big Game Awards held in 2001. Materials include correspondence, awardees lists, banquet invitations, planning and promotional materials, programs, and judging materials.
Created in 1948, the Sagamore Hill Medal is given by the Roosevelt family in honor of Theodore Roosevelt, Theodore Roosevelt, Jr., and Kermit Roosevelt. It is awarded by the Big Game Final Awards Judges panel to an outstanding trophy of distinction. Only one is given at any Big Game Awards Program and one need not be awarded at each Program. This Subseries contains certificates, correspondence and committee materials related to the Medal Program.
Official Measurers of the Boone and Crockett Club are volunteers who are certified by the Club to measure big game trophies. All trophies entered into a Records of North American Big Game Awards Program must be measured by a Boone and Crockett Club Official Measurer. Official Measurers have been utilized by the Boone and Crockett Club since the late 1940s.
This subseries contains correspondence between Official Measurers and Big Game Records professional staff, and the Records of North American Big Game Committee, and Official Measurer manual drafts. Of particular interest are materials related to Official Measurer training workshops developed by William H. Nesbitt, Administrative Director of the North American Big Game Records Program.
The National Collection of Heads and Horns was established by Club member William T. Hornaday and was displayed at the Bronx Zoo in New York City beginning in 1922. The collection is currently held at the Buffalo Bill Historical Center in Cody, Wyoming and is maintained by the Boone and Crockett Club.
This subseries contains correspondence, committee reports, inventories dating from 1906 through 1978, promotional materials, and trophy prints. Of particular interest are the research notes of Lowell E. Baier which provide a history of the National Collection of Heads and Horns.
This series documents the Boone and Crockett Club’s outreach, publicity, promotions and publications. The series has been divided into four subseries and includes correspondence, drafts of publications, materials related to the Club’s Fair Chase magazine, the Club’s newsletter, the Club’s Associate’s Program and licensing and copyright materials.
Materials in this series arrived at the archives with no discernable original order to the files and were grouped and interfiled by the processor to reflect historic and current organization of the Club’s communications division. Series are arranged alphabetically.
An Editorial Committee was formed at the first official meeting of the Boone and Crockett Club in 1888, and the Club has published materials related to big game, conservation, and hunting since 1893. This subseries contains five sub-subseries which include materials related to the Club’s published materials.
This sub-subseries contains materials created by both the Editorial and Historical committees of the Boone and Crockett Club from the late 1950s through the late 1980s, as well as materials created by paid professional staff. Items include committee meeting minutes, correspondence, book orders, inventories, and publication lists. Absent are materials related to items published before 1910.
This sub-subseries is divided into two sub-sub-subseries and contains materials related to the books published by the Boone and Crockett Club.
The first edition of Records of North American Big Game was published by the Club in 1932 in conjunction with the National Collection of Heads and Horns. After 1952 Records books were published every six to seven years. In 1993 it was determined that Records books would be published every six years.
This sub-sub-subseries contains materials from the first edition of Records of North American Big Game, published in 1932, through the tenth edition published in 1993. Materials include correspondence, drafts, signatures, proofs, and big game score charts.
In addition to the Records of North American Big Game books, the Boone and Crockett has published editions on wild sheep, record whitetail and mule deer as well as record elk. The club has also published books on hunting and conservation. This sub-sub-subseries contains correspondence, drafts, proofs, mailers and reviews related to these publications.
Established in 1994, Fair Chase magazine is distributed quarterly to Associate Members of the Club. This sub-subseries contains article drafts for the magazine and correspondence. Absent is a published run of the magazine.
This sub-subseries contains materials related to the Club’s newsletter that is distributed quarterly to regular members of the Club. Materials include correspondence and a run of the newsletters from 1985 through 2001.
This sub-subseries contains correspondence, drafts, and memoranda of miscellaneous volumes published by the Club.
The Boone and Crockett Club Associates Program was originally proposed by William I. Spencer in 1984. The program was developed to involve individuals who were interested in furthering the causes and work of the Club, but didn’t fit the requirements for regular membership as outlined in the Club’s constitution. An Associates Newsletter (which later developed into Fair Chase magazine) was developed to inform Associate Members of Club activities.
This subseries contains correspondence, candidate proposals, membership lists, and drafts and planning materials related to the Associates Newsletter.
This subseries contains correspondence, advertising, publicity and promotional materials and materials related to assignments of copyright. Of particular interest are assignments of copyright dating back to 1904.
This subseries contains correspondence, memoranda, and inquires related to Club films and miscellaneous materials.
In 1985 the Club formed the Boone and Crockett Club Foundation to manage and direct the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch. The Ranch was purchased by the Club to conduct research and educational activities related to big game and conservation. In 2009, all physical assets, including the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch, were transferred from the Foundation to the Club.
This series contains correspondence, the Foundation’s Board of Directors meeting minutes and by-laws, Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch materials, financial and fundraising documents, and materials related to the University of Montana Applied Research Program and Professorship.
Materials in this series arrived at the archives with no discernable original order to the files. Materials were grouped and interfiled by the processor to reflect historic organization of the Club’s Foundation. Series are arranged alphabetically and original order within folders was maintained.
This subseries contains annual meeting materials, correspondence, meeting minutes, and by-laws.
This Subseries contains correspondence arranged in alphabetical order. Of particular interest are folders containing the correspondence from Club member Sherman Gray as these folders demonstrate and document the development of the Foundation.
Purchased in 1985, the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch was purchased to conduct habitat and wildlife research and educational programs. The Ranch was formerly managed by the Boone and Crockett Club Foundation. In 2009, the Ranch, along with all other physical assets, was transferred to the Boone and Crockett Club.
This Subseries contains case statements, correspondence, donation data, member mailers, research reports, and materials created by the Ranch Management Committee.
In 1987 the Club entered into a collaboration with The University of Montana to establish and direct research programs at the Theodore Roosevelt Memorial Ranch. In addition, a Boone and Crockett Wildlife Professorship was established at the university.
This subseries contains the agreement with The University of Montana, correspondence, reports, and miscellaneous materials.
This subseries documents the fundraising activities of the Foundation. Included are audit materials, correspondence, donation reports, grant materials, financial documents, and tax materials.
This subseries contains articles, clippings, correspondence, and additional materials.
This series contains audiocassettes and VHS tapes that have not yet been identified.
This series consists of handwritten and typescript material produced by George Bird Grinnell and purchased from a manuscript dealer for the Boone and Crockett Club in 1999. The material is currently retained in its original notebook from the dealer.
The first folder contains correspondence from October 2, 1947 through September 10,1948, much of which was generated by S.R. Logan in his capacity as secretary of the Lake County Telephone Reorganization Committee, a few letters by Ray Sprague, chairman of the same group, and responses from individuals, government agencies, and businesses. The second folder contains items dated from January1946 to February 1948 that include legal documents, research on telephone associations, minutes of meetings, and expense records. The third folder contains polling or survey forms, used in March 1948 to determine the level of support on specific questions such as whether or not greatly expanded telephone service was needed and if telephone lines should be installed on power poles. The survey forms were sent to individuals, groups, and businesses.
This collection contains genealogical information on many branches from Fra Broadwell's family and Edwin Dana's family. There is correspondence from family members to Fra and Edwin about their families histories. Some of the families that have excellent research included are lines from the Anderson, Brewster, Broadwell, Dana, Forester, Maxwell, Page, Paine, Putnam, and Sunderland families, although this does not include all of the lines researched in this collection. There are copied accounts from family members early history, and publications on the Paine and Dana family.
Fra Dana also had publications on Astrology and scientific papers. There are also notes on the Crow language from Father Prando and Fra's own notes. Included also is a brand book of the cattle herd of the Blackfoot, which was purchased by E.L. Dana.
This series includes all of the genealogical information Fra Dana was able to gather on family descent. There are twenty-six families researched in this collection. Included is a direct line decent of Fra Broadwell Dana. There are several marriage certificates. These include the certificate for the marriage of John Sunderland to Elizabeth Page on February 14, 1819, a certificate for Samuel F. Maxwell and Eliza Ann Sunderland on November 8, 1848, a certificate for John W. Broadwell and Jewel H. Maxwell's marriage on May 12, 1873, and the marriage of E.L. Dana to Fra Broadwell on July 1, 1896. Parts of a will for E.L. Dana dated to 1916 are included and a copy of the will for Ann E. Broadwell dated to May 14, 1889, copied November 18, 1912 are included. There are also applications to the Daughters of the American Revolution for Jessie A. Sunderland (1899) and Emma R. Griffin (1909). The Paine and Dana lines also have published material on their families.
This series includes copies of accounts from early family history from various family members, such as H.W. Baldwin (1895-1897), M.A. Whipple (undated, 1935), Abraham Given (1850) and Theophilus and Debora Dana (1862). Poems written by E.L. Dana (published 1947) and Edna Dinwiddie (copy undated) are also included. There are copies of letters (undated, 1914, 1917-1918) from World War I and papers (1915, 1917, 1926) from World War I--correspondents are not identified by last name. There is a certificate from the Daughters of the American Revolution (D.A.R.) and Colonial Dames of America (undated, 1911-1912). Jewel Dinwiddie's Daughters of the American Revolution pin and tartan are in this collection as well. Family newspaper clippings are also included. This series also includes notes on the Crow language from Father Prando and Fra Dana and the brand book for the Blackfoot herd of cattle (undated).
This collection contains materials generated by Harry Fritz's time in the Montana Legislature as both a state representative and a state senator. This includes constituent correspondence, legislative information, notes, clippings, reports, news releases, campaign materials, legislative journals, and election materials from the 1980s and 1990s. The collection also includes office files from Fritz's forty year career with the Department of History at the University of Montana including lecture materials, research notes, articles, speaking engagement notes, calendars, Montana centennial materials, and manuscript reviews. The collection also includes several VHS tapes of presentations and events associated with the Montana State Legislature.
The collection includes a broad range of John Rankin's financial records, 1888-1906; speeches and clippings of Jeannette Rankin from 1916-1941, her 1940 congressional run, and a Report of International Congress of Women, 1919; and Wellington Rankin's 1946 campaign and two Montana Supreme Court cases, 1925 and 1941, in which he served, respectively, as attorney for the plaintiff and attorney for the defendant.
This series includes some financial records from Rankin's most notable endeavors such as the Rankin Block, the Rankin House, and lumber mills in Missoula. Those records pertain to day-to-day operating expenses and income. Two larger ledgers give a broader overview of Rankin's financial matters. Wherever possible the records have been arranged chronologically but gaps do exist.
This series includes the trail transcript for the 1925 Montana Supreme Court personal injury case of plaintiff, Velma H. Riggs, vs. defendant, Lew Webb. Wellington Rankin served as the attorney for plaintiff, Riggs. The series also includes the 1946 Montana Supreme Court decision in the case of A.E. Cramer vs. The Montana State Board of Food Distributors. Wellington Rankin served as an attorney for the defendants. The records of Wellington Rankin's 1948 congressional run include a pamphlet stating his platform and a copy of a speech by Senator Dan W. Maddox endorsing Rankin's candidacy.
This series includes a speech made by Jeannette Rankin on women's suffrage, excerpts from other Rankin speeches regarding Measures Touching the Interest of the People of Montana, a radio address on Women and Democracy by Rankin, and other speeches discussing defense issues. The series also includes additional miscellaneous material relating to Jeannette Rankin's 1940 congressional run. The Report of the International Congress of Women, which took place in Zurich in 1919, lists Jeannette Rankin as a delegate from the United States. This volume has sections in English, French, and German.
The collection consists of the personal records of Harry W. Child and the records of the Wylie Permanent Camping Company, Green Meadows Farm, the Yellowstone Park Association, Yellowstone Park Transportation Company, Yellowstone Park Company, Yellowstone Park Hotel Company, and Yellowstone Park Camping Company. It provides documentation of park visitors, employees, services, and the financial health of these companies.
This series contains Harry W. Child's personal account books. These contain financial records for his numerous real estate holdings in Helena and Toston, Montana; Gallatin Gateway, Montana; Gallatin and Madison Counties, Montana; and La Jolla, California. Many of the Helena records concern construction of a root cellar. Many records deal with Yellowstone Park ventures, including Yellowstone Park Transportation Company and Green Meadow Farm. There are extensive records of the activities of Child & Anceny, which dealt in real estate and cattle ranching in Montana. The volume of deeds and agreements concerns property transfers, many with the Northern Pacific Railroad. There is extensive correspondence with his Bozeman attorney, Hartman & Hartman.
This series contains a voucher register for the Wylie Permanent Camping Company, which consists of records of supplies purchased.
This series consists of a voucher register for Green Meadow Farm, which contains records for supplies purchased.
This series contains a voucher register for the Yellowstone Park Association, with record of supplies purchased.
This series contains the records of the Yellowstone Park Transportation Company, which provided first railroad and stagecoach service in the park, then automobile transport and services for visitors' automobiles. Filling station and garage records are for Mammoth, Old Faithful, Thumb, Lake, Fishing Bridge, and Canyon stations and show sales and the names of the operators. There is also a list of supplies and services available at these garages. The ledgers, journals, and voucher registers show operating expenses for the YPTC.
The last portion of the series consists of records of Park visitors from 1929 to 1951. The 1929-1930 book records visitors who entered the Park at West Yellowstone, Gardiner, and Gallatin Gateway by rail and lists them by state, town, and foreign country. The entrance registers, which run from 1946 to 1951, record visitors who entered the Park at Cody, Wyoming; Gardiner, Montana; Mammoth; Red Lodge, Montana; Gallatin Gateway, Montana; Victor, Wyoming; and West Yellowstone. Visitor information includes names, addresses, and fees paid for transportation or car rental.
This series contains records of the Yellowstone Park Company that do not fall under the purview of one of the subsidiary companies. It contains an employee register, fishing and boating records, a print shop inventory, and general ledgers. The employee registers list all YPC employees for the 1934 and 1935 seasons, their position, and whether they arrived by rail or automobile. There are both handwritten and typed versions of these records. Fishing and boating records show boat rentals and other types of sale at the docks at Lake, Fishing Bridge, Bridge Bay, and West Thumb. The general ledgers document purchases of supplies, construction materials, and telegraph and railway services, and document various other businesses operated in the Park.
This series contains records of the Yellowstone Park Hotel Company, which provided lodging services to Park visitors. The series consists of financial records that record the details of the Company's financial health. There is also a 1931 employee pay book from Mammoth, which lists employees by name and occupation.
This series contains the financial records of the Yellowstone Park Camping Company, which provided campgrounds to Park visitors.
This collection includes financial and legal records detailing the daily operations of a small-scale western Montana lumber mill, with particularly detailed records between 1944 and 1957. Most of the records are handwritten journals or logs recording aspects of mill operations such as log scale measurements submitted to the Montana State Forester for timber sale review, payroll hours and rates, and daily product and administrative transactions. Also included are typed records of quarterly production reports, timber sale agreements, and union relationships. The union contract records include correspondence regarding initial union representation for Morin Lumber Company employees.
This series includes a general equipment inventory, bound log scale books, small bound payroll logs, unbound production reports, small bound transaction journals, an unbound yard ledger, and five large bound ledgers of outgoing lumber sales. All records are handwritten except production reports, timber sale contracts, and union contracts. All bound transaction journals exhibit accounting shorthand practices. Log scale books record timber measurements submitted to the Montana State Forester as part of the timber sale review process. Payroll records detail compensation by individual per pay period, including per diem totals. Production reports detail lumber production totals, equipment purchases, outgoing shipments, existing stock arranged by tree species, and production lost to injury. General Accounts Journals record daily transactions, credits, debts, and deposits. The yard ledger is an alphabetized record of account activities from the Miller Creek mill operation. Cash Books record sales of lumber leaving the processing yard.
This series includes records detailing timber sale agreements and union relationships. All timber contract records detail locations, total board feet, and compensation. Most contracts in this collection were between Morin Lumber Company and the State of Montana. Union contracts materials primarily record personnel allocation agreements but also include official correspondence between employees, union representatives, and mill ownership regarding the initiation of union representation. All records are typed and in good condition.
This collection contains documents that span from McCormick's early days in Montana to after his death and the settling of his estate. Many are legal documents from the firm of Higgins and McCormick, which was in business until his death in 1889. Included in the collection are several receipts, letters, and official documents pertaining to McCormick's estate, which was managed by his wife Kate and son, W. J. McCormick, Jr.
The collection contains general correspondence, financial records, legal documents and maps from 1945 to 1971.
The series consists of reminder letters concerning unpaid bills from other companies, workman's compensation claims, copies of outgoing correspondence and information on timber products.
The series contains check registers, payroll information, assets and liabilities balance sheets, tax returns, and time sheets from Cottrell and Helean Logging Company. Log hauling reports, which contain the car number, number of logs hauled, number of board feet, and totals is in the series. Also in the series is wage schedules that specifies all grades of a certain logging job and the wage scale for that position. A general ledger containing assets and liabilities of the company and two payroll registers, including a saw scale, are in the series.

The series consists of unit maps that show the certain areas that the company logged. The five maps in the series are of the Hyde, Fish and Granite Creek areas, and two from the Big Blackfoot Milling Company.
The collection contains financial records including volumes for price lists, engraver's records, outside and Butte shipping slips from 1926 to 1966.
The series contains volumes of price list records, engraver's records, outside shipping slips (for items shipped outside Butte), and Butte shipping slips (for items shipped within Butte). The price lists detail the description of the headstone, including the dimensions and the price that was charged to the buyer. The volumes also include the name of the purchaser, the date that the stone was processed and the time spent working on it. The volumes are arranged alphabetically by the company's sizing system. The series also contains the engraver's records which correspond to the records kept in the price list volumes.
The volumes are organized by the job number of the stone. Outside shipping slips are organized by the city in which the completed stone was sent, such as Anaconda, Deer Lodge, Dillon, Helena, Idaho, and other outside states. The records are organized by work number and include the name of the deceased with the birth and death dates, the purchaser of the stone, and the date when the order was paid in full. The shipper's name and address and shipment date, and a detailed description of the stone are also in the outside shipping slips. The Butte shipping slips contain the same information on them as in the outside shipping slips except the name of the cemetery is included. The volumes are arranged by name of cemetery, including Holy Cross, Mountain View, Mountain Moriah, St. Patrick, and UG Weeks.
James H. Morley's daily dairy accounts from 1862-1865 begin with his trip to Montana from St. Louis, Missouri, onboard a steamer up the Missouri River. It continues with his group's two week journey from Fort Benton to their camp and mining site on Gold Creek, between what is now Drummond and Deer Lodge, Montana, with supply loaded wagons. From that point his diary entries describe the day's shaft or sluice mining efforts, reports from group members who had traveled to other possible mining sites, and descriptions of his own travels around Hellgate Canyon and into Rock Creek, then on to Beaverhead, Flint Creek, Wisdom River, the Big Hole prairie, and back up to Deer Lodge Creek. By January 1863 Morley and his team had ranged as far east in Montana as the Gallatin and Three Forks areas. Also in January Morley noted the results of a trial of Plummer, probably the infamous Harry Plummer, one year before that man was hung by vigilantes without a trial. Morley briefly describes his own contact with justice as a juror in a trial of accused murderer Bill Mitchell.
Over the next two years Morley sometimes described the daily drudgery of mining work but also mining claim disputes, planning and charting a plat map for Centreville, wildlife and geological features, scouting for and staking new claims, difficulties of sending and receiving mail, and the mining towns of Bannack and Virginia City, Montana. His daily entries end with his return to St. Louis in August, 1865.
This collection includes a photocopy of Helen Edna Buck's thirty-two page, handwritten letter to Clara Ballard (addressed as Dear Friend) detailing her family's move from Yakima, Washington to Rhodes, Iowa. Buck describes the weather, roads, camp sites and camping conditions, livestock and wildlife encounters, interesting geology, towns and people they encountered. The towns in Montana included Saltese, St. Regis, Huson, Missoula, Butte, Whitehall, Custer, Miles City, Glendive, and Wibaux. Their route included the road called the Camel's Hump. She also writes of going through Yellowstone Park, car trouble, and how she felt about her new home.
John Well-Off-Man's Collection of Photographs contains 109 images of people and events on the Rocky Boy's Indian Reservation. The photographs were taken during the late nineteenth and early twentieth centuries. Well-Off-Man collected these images from Paul Mitchell, an elder from Rocky Boy's Indian Reservation, as part of his research into the history of the Rocky Boy Reservation. Well-Off-Man made copy negatives from Mitchell's nitrate negatives.
A portion of the images in this collection have brief descriptions written on them, though it is not clear by whom. Almost all the images are undated and many currently lack identification of the individuals in them. Most are of Cree and Ojibwe (Chippewa) people. While the images in the collection come from several sources, the majority were likely taken by John Gable, the son of William Gable who was the Lutheran Pastor on the Rocky Boy Reservation in the 1920s, 30s, and 40s. As a graduate student at the Philadelphia Seminary in the 1930s, John Gable was also responsible for a number of film productions including "Rocky Boy Mission In Action," a 1935 film about the Lutheran Mission on the Rocky Boy Reservation. While it is unclear whether the photos in this collection are associated with Gable's documentary project, the content of the images suggest that there is a connection between the two. According to Well-Off-Man other images were taken by Florence Bruckner.
This collection contains materials related to the development, operation and dismantling of the Douglas Mine and Concentrator, located in Granite County, Montana, by the Montana Phosphate Products Company and Cominco American, Inc. during the 1960s and early 1970s. The records offers insight into mining philosophies and trends of that time, as well as providing information on the day-to-day operations of a phosphate mine and milling operation in Western Montana.
Series I, Mine and Concentrator Development, contains materials related to the development of the Douglas Operation by the Montana Phosphate Products Company, and later Cominco American, Inc., beginning in 1962 and extending into mid-1960s. Included are cost quotations and advertisements for various mining and milling equipment, engineering drawings, construction specifications, cost projections and other materials. This series gives an overview of state-of-the-art phosphate mining technologies in the 1960s, as well as the amount of financial investment and work necessary to undertake such a mining project.
Series II, Mine and Concentrator Operations, contains daily and monthly reports, maintenance schedules, studies, correspondence, financial calculations, and other miscellaneous materials created by the Montana Phosphate Products Company and Cominco American, Inc. during the operation of the Douglas Mine and Concentrator from 1962-1968. This material provides a look into the day-to-day operations of a phosphate mine and concentrator operating in Western Montana during the 1960s.
Series III, Concentrator Dismantling, contains correspondence and daily reports, as well as other miscellaneous material related to the dismantling of the Douglas Concentrator in 1972. This action was authorized by Cominco American, Inc. and carried out by the Bechtel Corporation. The series is representative of how Cominco American, Inc. was able to salvage much of the equipment at its Douglas Creek location for use in another mining project in Greenland.
Series IV, Maps and Drawings, contains numerous oversized maps and drawings depicting the Douglas Operation and other Montana Phosphate Products Company and Cominco American, Inc. mines in the region, including the Anderson (Warm Springs), Brock, Luke, and Relyea Mines. The materials range in subject from underground mines to dam cross-sections to construction specifications.
The Peggy DeMichele papers contain photos, speeches, and documents of Montana Congressman James O’Connor, with whom DeMichele worked prior to Mike Mansfield, as well as her personal ephemera and photos.
This collection contains letters from customers throughout Montana and nearby states ordering fruit from Theon H. Durnford in Lolo, Montana, 1913-1924, with the bulk from 1918, and Durnford's receipts and statements from Hughes Mercantile of Lolo, Montana, from 1917-1919.The bulk of the letters are orders for Theon H. Dunford’s fruit but a few letters also contain personal, cultural, and social information on topics including the influenza epidemic, the scarcity of workers during the First World War, and oil drilling. The letters also offer information about the varieties of fruit Durnford grew, how these fruits were shipped, how customers chose to use the products, and how a small agricultural business functioned at the time. Durnford shipped his fruit both to individual customers and retail distributors. Many of his customers were in Big Timber, Three Forks, Toston, and Townsend, Montana.
The receipts and invoices from Hughes Mercantile record Durnford's sale of eggs to the store in exchange for everything from laundry to canned peas and chicken feed.
Receipts and statements for items bought and sold at Hughes Mercantile in Lolo, Montana.

The album also contains a few family photos of John M. Clifton, his wife Nora Toole Clifton, and their baby daughter, Thula Clifton.

This collection contains materials related to the research and writing of Oberdorfer’s book, Senator Mansfield: The Extraordinary Life of a Great American Statesman and Diplomat (Smithsonian Books, 2003), which won the D.B. Hardeman Prize in 2003. The book is a biography of Mike Mansfield, a United States House Representative and Senator from Montana who also served as ambassador to Japan during the Carter and Reagan administrations. The collection provides access to the documents and other materials that Oberdorfer cites in his book, Senator Mansfield. The research materials include photocopies and summaries from books and articles about Mansfield and related historical topics, as well as primary documents gathered from archival repositories like the presidential libraries of John F. Kennedy and Lyndon B. Johnson. The research materials provide glimpses into Mansfield’s personal life and public career through copies of correspondence, photographs, and other materials from the private collections of Mansfield family members.
The collection includes summaries of Oberdorfer’s conversations with Mansfield’s family, colleagues, and friends and some drafts of chapters from Oberdorfer’s book. Manuscript drafts and writings related to the book are filed with the research materials. The collection also contains recorded interviews with Mansfield and Mansfield's colleagues that Oberdorfer conducted as research for the Mansfield biography, as well as non-interview audio recordings related to Oberdorfer's research.
The collection includes summaries of Oberdorfer’s conversations with Mansfield’s family, colleagues, and friends and some drafts of chapters from Oberdorfer’s book. Manuscript drafts and writings related to the book are filed with the research materials.

These audio interviews were assigned an oral history collection name, Don Oberdorfer Interviews with Mike Mansfield Oral History Project and given collection number OH 391, to facilitate discovery and access.
There is no recorded audio OH 391-001 cassette tape. The interview consists of Don Oberdorfer’s notes taken during his first unrecorded meetings with Mansfield about the biography. A full transcript of these notes is available on ScholarWorks.

The collection contains a variety of materials collected and produced by Haugland as part of his journalism career, personal writing, and enduring interest in the military. Correspondence from his career was mostly conducted for research purposes and includes exchanges with many military personnel. Writings include manuscripts of articles, including those written for the Associated Press and his novel. There are financial materials related to his many travels for his work, along with his travel documents like passports. There are research materials related to NASA and the space program, as well as K'tut Tantri in Indonesia. There are clippings of many of his articles, some personal materials, and memorabilia. Last, there are photographs of Haugland and that he collected for his work.
The series contains correspondence that Haugland conducted with various people throughout his career with the Associated Press and into his retirement. Haugland conducted correspondence with his research subjects, including the Eagles, an American World War II flying force fighting for Britain before America entered the war, and K'tut Tantri, and Indonesian women who Haugland made the subject for one of his manuscripts. Haugland also corresponded with Great Britain's Prince Philip in his research of the Eagles, who made him an honorary member of their group. Haugland had a great deal of correspondence with book companies who wanted Haugland to write for them. He also corresponded with military personnel, many of whom were personal friends of Haugland's because of his NASA splashdown coverage for the AP.
The series is divided into two subseries: Manuscripts and Datelines. The first portion is manuscripts of articles and his novel manuscripts. The second part of the series is Haugland's datelines that he wrote for the AP. Many articles that Haugland wrote dealt with the avionics industry, including airplanes, military bombers and the NASA space exploration. He also wrote many articles and two books on the experience of the Eagles during WWII. Copies of his manuscripts of Eagle Squadron and The Eagle's War are in the series. Many of his research notes are also included. Another book manuscript, Revolt in Paradise, is in the series. The datelines are mainly written about the avionics industry. Many news stories are about NASA and the different space missions, including the Apollo and Gemini flights. Other news stories on which Haugland reported were events in the Soviet Union, Vietnam, Japan, and the South Pacific.
The series contains general and travel receipts from the many locations in which Haugland traveled to for the Associated Press. Also in the series are his expense accounts and tax information, including tax returns. The series is arranged in two parts. The first part, general financial records, is arranged chronologically.
The series consists mainly of documents from Haugland's years as a war correspondent. They include his license, passports, war correspondent agreement contract, orders, a permit to leave the United States, and an Australian registration. Other documents in the series are agreements with publishing companies for Haugland's manuscripts, such as Harper and Brothers and Spartan Books.
The series contains materials that Haugland used in research for his articles. The majority of research materials are about NASA and the space program. Haugland covered the Apollo missions, Gemini and Voyager. Other topics that Haugland researched were the places he traveled, military, and K'tut Tantri in Indonesia.
